<div id="review_1781610014" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1781610014" />
    <a title="Leona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30885832-leona"><img alt="Leona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027461p2/30885832.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1781610014?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leona" href="/user/show/30885832-leona">Leona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17227253-tiger-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30885832-leona?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1781610014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6919433316725686252">I knew if I just kept working my way through this series that I would find a story that would leave me speechless, and <strong>
  <em>Tiger Magic</em>
</strong> was that story.<br/><br/>I have always had a weakness for tiger shifters. I don’t know if it’s because of the rarity that these type of shifters are featured or because of the tiger’s nature, but you can always put me down for a tiger shifter story any day of the week!<br/><br/>When I had read the synopsis for <strong>
  <em>Tiger Magic</em>
</strong> a while back, I knew that I had to read it, but sadly my </span>
  <span id="freeText6919433316725686252" style="display:none">I knew if I just kept working my way through this series that I would find a story that would leave me speechless, and <strong>
  <em>Tiger Magic</em>
</strong> was that story.<br /><br />I have always had a weakness for tiger shifters. I don’t know if it’s because of the rarity that these type of shifters are featured or because of the tiger’s nature, but you can always put me down for a tiger shifter story any day of the week!<br /><br />When I had read the synopsis for <strong>
  <em>Tiger Magic</em>
</strong> a while back, I knew that I had to read it, but sadly my library didn’t have it available yet. In the flow of life and obligations I sort of forgot about it. It was when I saw that <strong>
  <em>Tiger Magic</em>
</strong> was finally available that I didn’t even need to have a look at the other books in this series, I knew that this one was for me.<br /> From the first page to its last, <strong><em>Tiger Magic</em></strong> was amazing. It’s different when you read the synopsis and know that it’s going to be a good story, and then you read it and you’re still like, “Wow.” <br />The personality of Tiger and his relationship with Carly was so magnetic that despite how I felt about the other characters in <strong>
  <em>Tiger Magic</em>
</strong> I was 100% rooting for them to succeed in whatever they felt they needed to do in order for Tiger to be left alone and to live in peace. While both wanted peace and a sense of belonging they wren’t willing to fall on their swords to make it happen either. Their ‘us against the world’ mentality throughout this story really brought a lot of the flaws that these Shiftertowns have out into the open, on top of the restrictions they heap upon themselves when there could very well be better alternatives.<br /><br />I loved everything about <strong>
  <em>Tiger Magic</em>
</strong> and I really had wished that it hadn’t ended, I would’ve loved to have seen their bundle of joy come into the world and Tiger’s response to him. This story gripped me and never let me go, and I was a willing captive. I have a few more stories from this series waiting in my queue that I can’t wait to get to, so hopefully we can continue on with the great momentum that <strong>
  <em>Tiger Magic</em>
</strong> gave.<br /><br /><strong>P.S. Does Spike have a book?</strong><br />***Originally reviewed at Literary Treasure Chest: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.literarytreasurechest.com/books/tiger-magic-jennifer-ashley/">http://www.literarytreasurechest.com/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6919433316725686252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1180023870" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1180023870" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4731410-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387526203p2/4731410.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1180023870?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/4731410-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=huge-hero">huge-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=fated-mates">fated-mates</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=pregnancy">pregnancy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=feline-shifters">feline-shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=tortured-hero">tortured-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=genetic-engineering">genetic-engineering</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1180023870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer961603658752367157"><b>Tiger Magic</b><br/>4 Stars<br/><br/>Rescued from horrific experiments and relocated to the shiftertown in Austin, Tiger, a rare bengal shifter, feels like an outcast until the day he stumbles across Carly Randal broken down on the side of a deserted road, and knows he has met his mate. As Carly is slowly drawn into the dangers and intrigues of the shifter world, her one constant is the intensity of her feelings for Tiger. But will that be enough to overcome the obstacles in their path to happiness?<br/><br/>A sweet additio</span>
  <span id="freeText961603658752367157" style="display:none"><b>Tiger Magic</b><br />4 Stars<br /><br />Rescued from horrific experiments and relocated to the shiftertown in Austin, Tiger, a rare bengal shifter, feels like an outcast until the day he stumbles across Carly Randal broken down on the side of a deserted road, and knows he has met his mate. As Carly is slowly drawn into the dangers and intrigues of the shifter world, her one constant is the intensity of her feelings for Tiger. But will that be enough to overcome the obstacles in their path to happiness?<br /><br />A sweet addition to the series.<br /><br />Tiger and Carly are incredible together. Carly is openminded and loyal to a fault. Her love, trust and acceptance of him despite his fearsome visage is heartwarming. That said, the ease and speed with which she accepts Tiger and the other shifters into her life does require a certain suspension of disbelief, but that goes without saying given the paranormal genre. <br /><br />Tiger is an amazing mix of intense strength and incredible innocence and vulnerability. On the one hand, he is personifies the threat and the danger inherent to the shifters, but on the other, he has such a magnificent heart and capacity for love. It is impossible not to feel for his suffering and root for his happiness. <br /><br />As the setting is once again the shiftertown in Austin, Texas, we are treated to updates in the lives of the characters from the first two installments. Liam and Kim, Sean and Andrea, Dylan and Glory, and a host of others all put in an appearance and flesh out the secondary cast. Although I’ve not read any of the novellas, it is easy to follow the characters and the developments in their lives. <br /><br />The plot revolving around the conflicting agendas of the various groups interested in Tiger’s true nature whether for good or for evil makes for interesting and suspenseful reading. There is, however, one plot point that doesn’t make sense and puts a small damper on the believability of the ending - why would <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the scientists put Tiger through such excruciating experiments if their aim was to create a search and rescue shifter? It just doesn’t jive. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />All in all, an enjoyable read and I’m glad I didn’t give up on the series after the disappointment of book #3. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="961603658752367157" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1117350918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6313849997989312045">Re-read<br/>I liked Tiger and felt for him from the moment Iona saved him. His story was heartbreaking: a shifter created in a secret laboratory and kept there (area 51) for 40 years or so. He was tortured and experimented on for the good of science.<br/>From the beginning, the shifters didn't know what to do and how to deal with Tiger but Dylan saw something in him and took him to his town. <br/><br/>While the shifters didn't know what to do with him and how to control him, their children/ cubs knew better. They t</span>
  <span id="freeText6313849997989312045" style="display:none">Re-read<br />I liked Tiger and felt for him from the moment Iona saved him. His story was heartbreaking: a shifter created in a secret laboratory and kept there (area 51) for 40 years or so. He was tortured and experimented on for the good of science.<br />From the beginning, the shifters didn't know what to do and how to deal with Tiger but Dylan saw something in him and took him to his town. <br /><br />While the shifters didn't know what to do with him and how to control him, their children/ cubs knew better. They trusted and liked Tiger, and he was very protective of them.<br />When Tiger met Carly he knew she is his mate and stayed with her all the way.<br />Carly had a good life but Tiger opened up a world of possibilities and adventures for her. Her attraction was instant but her love for Tiger grew in time and that was great for the whole story.<br /><br />I loved the fact that Tiger was indeed special and now he had someone in his life to love and love him back. He was not just genetically enhanced but he had a new set of powers that set him aside from all other shifters.<br /><br />The whole book kept me on my toes with all the troubles that Tiger went through in finding his peace and place among shifters and humans. <br />I would have thought that the shifters after being marginalized and considered second class citizens by humans and animals by Fae would have had more compassion and understanding for Tiger. It was not the case and that was sad.<br />In the end, Tiger got his HEA with Carly and a cub on the way.<br /><br />My favorite story for far.<br /> <br /><br /><br /></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2225246-darcy?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7368165666419968751">I was so happy when I realized that this book centered around Tiger. From the start I liked him, hated how his life started out, but loved that with Liam and the Austin Shiftertown he had a chance at a real life.<br/><br/>I loved how Tiger recognized Carly as his mate right away. I thought it was funny how even though he kept stating the fact around Carly she didn't realize the implications. I also really loved that Carly was the one person to calm Tiger down. It was great to how the other shifters reacte</span>
  <span id="freeText7368165666419968751" style="display:none">I was so happy when I realized that this book centered around Tiger. From the start I liked him, hated how his life started out, but loved that with Liam and the Austin Shiftertown he had a chance at a real life.<br /><br />I loved how Tiger recognized Carly as his mate right away. I thought it was funny how even though he kept stating the fact around Carly she didn't realize the implications. I also really loved that Carly was the one person to calm Tiger down. It was great to how the other shifters reacted to this.<br /><br />I think the best trait that Carly has was her acceptance of Tiger and how she defended him, even against other shifters. I was glad that Tiger finally had someone in his corner. You would think that the other shifters would accept him instead they feared him when they shouldn't have. They should have trusted his actions, which have always been to protect those weaker than him.<br /><br />I was intrigued by how the Shifter Bureau played into things. I hated how things started out with them, but loved how things ended. It is a great start to better acceptance for the Shifters. </span>

<div id="review_646613516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer15897319900391633498">I have a mixed relationship with this series. I liked the first book, but found only ok the second. And I couldn't get interested into the sequels. <br/><br/>Tiger Magic came to my attention from friends' reviews.   <span id="freeText15897319900391633498" style="display:none">I have a mixed relationship with this series. I liked the first book, but found only ok the second. And I couldn't get interested into the sequels. <br /><br />Tiger Magic came to my attention from friends' reviews. They all love this series and I thought to give it a try again.<br /><br />Tiger Magic is simply too bland for my tastes. I liked seeing what happened to characters I had already met. But I wasn't that intrigued by Tiger, his story, his mate. <br /><br />The story was too sugary for me. Plus, I found his background pretty unbelievable. You either follow Sci-Fi or Fantasy, a mix of the two has to be really strong. Here we are simply told that we have the capacity of engineering a complete new species, from scratches. As a final nail in the coffin, the supposed "good research" is pretty hilarious. They basically tortured him so he could be a good search dog. Sorry, the killing machine was much more believable. </span>

  <span id="freeText332626819134593820" style="display:none">The first few paragraphs of this book made me skeptical i could come to like the heroine but she actually turned out to be one of my favorites in the series thus far. I was really curious about tiger after the last book and even more excited to go back to the austin shiftertown. I didn't actively dislike 3&amp;4 but for some reason I just didn't get as emotionally involved with the vegas shifters. Tiger was an oddity, i really liked him but i feel like portions of his character was underdeveloped. He learned english from his tormentors in a clinical setting and some colloquialisms from other shifters but he was able to offer a heartfelt i love you? how was he able to know the words, understand they were important, and deliver them with the emotion of someone who would've grown up hearing heartfelt i love yous? Also the climactic scene was a little underdeveloped. Where was tiger in the time he was missing? how did he get back so fast? how did he know there was trouble? Other than certain portions of tiger himself and that particular scene being underdeveloped i really loved this book. Tiger was equal parts sweet and fiercely protective. It did bother me that no one gave him a real name...almost like they tried to avoid humanizing him. Carly was a firecracker. For all that my first impression of her was pampered rich bitch she turned into tiger's biggest ally and a really amusing character. I thought the romance happened a little fast but it worked and the sex scenes were very nsfw. The overall plot of the series got more interesting but the lineup of future books characters isn't very inspiring to me so i may put the rest off for a bit and come back to them at some later point.</span>
  <a data-text-id="332626819134593820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
